InVivoStat Repeated Measures Parametric Analysis

Response and covariance structure

The Resp12 response is currently being analysed by the Repeated Measures Parametric Analysis module.

The response has been arcsine transformed prior to analysis.

The repeated measures mixed model analysis is using the compound symmetric covariance structure to model the within-subject correlations. When using this structure you are assuming sphericity and also that the variability of responses is the same at each level of Day3, see Pinherio and Bates (2002). These assumptions may not hold in practice.

The analysis implements the Kenward-Roger approximation of the degress of freedom, Kenward and Roger (1997).

Comment: The overall tests in this table are marginal likelihood ratio tests, where the order they appear in the table does not influence the results.

Conclusion: There are no statistically significant overall differences, at the 5% level, between the levels of any of the terms in the table of overall tests.

Tip: While it is a good idea to consider the overall tests in the above table, we should not rely on them when deciding whether or not to make pairwise comparisons.

Diagnostic plots

Residuals vs. predicted plot

Tip: On this plot look to see if the spread of the points increases as the predicted values increase. If so the response may need transforming.

Tip: Any observation with a standardised residual less than -3 or greater than 3 (SD) should be investigated as a possible outlier.

Comment: The standardised residuals are obtained by subtracting the fitted values from the responses and dividing by the estimated within-group standard error.

Normal probability plot

Tip: Check that the points lie along the dotted line. If not then the data may be non-normally distributed.

( A , W , '3' , c , D3 ) - ( B , W , '3' , c , D3 ) 0.382 -0.291 1.056 0.34 0.2630

Analysis description

The data were analysed using a 5-way repeated measures mixed model approach, with Treat17, Treat18, Treat19 and Treat20 as treatment factors and Day3 as the repeated factor. This was followed by Planned Comparisons on the predicted means to compare the levels of the effect Treat17 * Treat18 * Treat19 * Treat20 * Day3. The response was arcsine transformed prior to analysis to stabilise the variance.

The compound symmetric covariance structure was used to model the within-subject correlations. When using this structure we assumed that the variability of the responses was the same at each level of Day3 and the correlation between responses from any pair of levels of Day3 is the same.

The analysis implements the Kenward-Roger adjustment to the degrees of freedom, Kenward and Roger (1997).

A full description of mixed model theory can be found in Venables and Ripley (2003) and Pinherio and Bates (2002).

For more information on the theoretical approaches that are implemented within this module, see Bate and Clark (2014).

Venables, W.N. and Ripley, B.D. (2003). Modern Applied Statistics with S. 4th Edition; Springer. New York, Inc.
